**Production reliability — hotfix (logged + closed 2026-05-06 in v3.8.aah, Sprint 29):**

33. ~~**RateConfirmation modal accessorial shape mismatch — same root-cause class as Item 32 Load Board crash, different surface.**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-06 in v3.8.aah** (Sprint 29 hotfix immediately after Sprint 28 Phase A surfaced it as A28-1 P0). Phase A static-analysis grep on `frontend/src/` for accessorial render sites surfaced [`RateConfirmationModal.tsx:418`](frontend/src/components/loads/RateConfirmationModal.tsx#L418) — pre-fix code: `description: a.description || a` fell through `|| a` to the whole `{type, amount, payer}` Order Builder object when `.description` was undefined. Object then propagated to (1) [`line 500`](frontend/src/components/loads/RateConfirmationModal.tsx#L500) `.filter((a) => a.description.trim())` → TypeError "a.description.trim is not a function"; (2) [`line 1716-1717`](frontend/src/components/loads/RateConfirmationModal.tsx#L1716) `<input value={acc.description} ... />` → React error #31 same as Sprint 26b. **Trigger conditions** identical to Item 32: load created via Order Builder convert flow + at least one accessorial added + AE opens RateConfirmation modal. **Fix** — defensive type-check pattern matching Sprint 26b. Three input shapes supported: string (legacy) → description = a; `{description, amount}` (RC's own saved shape from prior RC modal saves) → description = a.description; `{type, amount, payer}` (Order Builder shape per [`orders/types.ts:90`](frontend/src/app/dashboard/orders/types.ts#L90)) → description = a.type. Order Builder accessorial `{type: "Detention", amount: 0}` now hydrates as RC modal accessorial `{description: "Detention", amount: "0"}`. **Why Phase A caught it that Sprint 26b's frontend smoke didn't:** Sprint 26b smoke clicked Load Board side panel which doesn't open the RC modal — the RC modal is opened separately via "Send Rate Confirmation" action on a tendered load. The bug shape was identical but on a different render site. Sprint 28's static-analysis grep for accessorial readers surfaced this immediately, validating the audit-only sprint methodology. **Root-cause loophole still open (Sprint 31 candidate):** [`backend/src/validators/load.ts:113`](backend/src/validators/load.ts#L113) `accessorials: z.array(z.any()).optional()` accepts any shape — Sprint 26b + Sprint 29 both cosmetically patched consumer sides but Order Builder writes its shape and RC modal save writes its shape, so multiple shapes coexist in DB. Sprint 31 will tighten the validator + add data migration. Sprint 29 handles both shapes defensively at read time. **Pre-commit verification:** backend `tsc --noEmit` clean (no backend changes), frontend `next build` clean. Net LOC change: ~15 (1 file, accessorial hydrator block expanded from 1 line to ~17 with defensive type-check + comment block). Per §3.1 sequence-continuous rule: v3.8.aag → v3.8.aah. Logged + closed in same commit per established hotfix-with-immediate-close pattern.

**Sprint 52 epic — tender workflow polish (banked §19 meta-50, 2026-05-16, post-Sprint-50 v3.8.abn session arc closure):**

141. **Tender expiry cron sweeper.** Logged 2026-05-16 §19 meta-50. Today `LoadTender.expiresAt` is enforced at validator write time (Sprint 44d Item 78) and surfaced in the RC PDF banner (Sprint 48 Item 108) but no background job sweeps past-expiry tenders. AE Console relies on the 30-second `refetchInterval` polling (Sprint 36 Item 50) to surface stale tenders, and the tender-decline email path (Sprint 45a `sendTenderExpiredEmail`, Item 80) has no firing trigger. **Sprint shape:** node-cron tick every 10 minutes that selects OFFERED tenders with `expiresAt < now`, flips status → EXPIRED, fires `notifyTenderAction(tender.id, "EXPIRED")`, advances any waterfall position to next-tier carrier where applicable. ~40 LOC across `backend/src/services/cronService.ts` (or new file) + tenderController helper. Sub-rule c gates: verify cron runtime (Render service supports cron via setInterval or external scheduler), authoritative-source check on EXPIRED status state machine downstream consumers. **Sprint 52a.** Not BKN-blocking — manual AE intervention works pre-cron; cron adds reliability + closes Item 80's defensive function reaching live state.

142. **Magic-link carrier accept-without-login.** Logged 2026-05-16 §19 meta-50. Today `sendTenderOfferedEmail` (Sprint 45a Item 80) lands in carrier inbox with a CTA pointing at `/carrier/dashboard/tenders` — carrier must log in to act. Industry-best brokers (CHR, Coyote, RXO, Convoy) all support magic-link accept/decline embedded in the tender email itself, removing the login friction class. **Sprint shape:** generate per-tender signed JWT (24h expiry) embedding `{tenderId, action: accept|decline}`; render two CTA buttons in `sendTenderOfferedEmail` ("Accept this load" / "Decline"); new public route `GET /api/tender-action/:token` verifies JWT, applies action, returns acknowledgment page (frontend route `/tender-action/[token]/page.tsx` or static HTML). Carriers can accept while driving / between loads / off-laptop. ~80-100 LOC across 4 files (token generator + email CTA + public endpoint + acknowledgment page). Sub-rule c gates: authoritative-source check on JWT lifecycle (matches existing `tracking` token pattern at Sprint 47.b Item 31 close), audit-both-ends-of-data-flow verify acknowledgment page can mutate tender status without auth context. **Sprint 52b.** Highest UX leverage item in tender workflow polish — drops tender acceptance latency from minutes to seconds.

143. **Counter-tender email handler.** Logged 2026-05-16 §19 meta-50. Originally banked as Item 89 (Sprint 45a) for Sprint 45b. Sprint 45b never materialized; counter-tender email path remains unfired. `notifyTenderAction("COUNTERED")` currently writes only the in-app `Notification` record; carrier-side counter-offer (currently no frontend UI to submit) and AE-side counter-receive (no email) both gaps. **Sprint shape:** (a) `sendTenderCounteredEmail` function in `emailService.ts` — AE-facing email when carrier counters; carrier-counter-offer requires frontend UI work which is Item 144 scope; (b) extend `notifyTenderAction` COUNTERED case to fire the email. ~25 LOC. **Sprint 52c.** Pairs with Items 142 + 144 — magic-link flow could embed counter UI inline.

144. **Tiered expiry preset UX (4h / 24h / 48h).** Logged 2026-05-16 §19 meta-50. Originally Item 77 (Sprint 44d) — AE Tender modal has no UI to set tender expiry; defaults to 24h hardcoded fallback. Industry pattern (TQL, Echo, Landstar) all expose expiry presets in the tender creation surface — 4-hour for urgent loads, 24-hour standard, 48-hour for flexible-window loads. Schema already supports custom `expiresAt` (Sprint 44d). **Sprint shape:** add 3-button preset toggle to Tender modal (`/dashboard/loads` page Tender form) + custom-expiry input fallback; wire into createTender mutation body to override the hardcoded 24h fallback. ~40 LOC. Sub-rule c gate: audit-both-ends-of-data-flow verify preset writes through validator (`expiresAt: z.string().transform(s => new Date(s))` already accepts arbitrary ISO strings, no validator change needed). **Sprint 52d.** Pairs with Sprint 45b ghost — closes the user's "optimal workflow" four-step spec retroactively.

87.b. **`LoadTender.declineReason` field + capture flow** (closes Item 87 schema gap; extends Item 90). Logged 2026-05-16 §19 meta-50. Today `LoadTender` schema has no `declineReason` field (Item 90 verification, Sprint 45a). `sendTenderDeclinedEmail` always passes `declineReason: undefined`; the conditional rendering (Sprint 45a D4) gracefully omits the row, but the AE-facing email reads "Tender declined by {carrier}" with no reason context. **Sprint shape:** (a) add `declineReason String?` to `LoadTender` schema migration, (b) extend `declineTender` controller to read `req.body.reason` (~5 LOC), (c) extend carrier portal `/carrier/dashboard/tenders` decline modal to capture reason — categorized dropdown (Rate too low / Capacity full / Lane mismatch / Equipment unavailable / Other) + free-text fallback, (d) magic-link decline flow (Item 142) inherits the reason capture via embedded JSON. ~80-120 LOC across 4 files + 1 migration. **Sprint 52e.** Item identifier `87.b` rather than 87 (Item 87 is the unrelated `emailTemplates.ts` wrapper consolidation). Pairs naturally with Items 142 + 143 — magic-link counter UI from Sprint 52b/c could embed decline-reason capture in the same flow.

145. **Engagement signals + decline taxonomy analytics.** Logged 2026-05-16 §19 meta-50. Post-Sprint-52a-d, the platform will have rich tender lifecycle data (offered → opened → accepted/declined/expired/countered + decline reasons via Item 87.b). Build the analytics surface: tender-funnel conversion rate by carrier / lane / equipment / day-of-week / hour-of-day; decline reason distribution by carrier tier + lane; AE expiry-preset effectiveness (4h vs 24h vs 48h acceptance rate). **Sprint shape:** Analytics dashboard under `/admin/analytics` (new tab or extension of existing). ~150 LOC across charts + aggregation queries. Sub-rule c gates: Pattern 7 design-system conformance audit (analytics surface across drawer + chart conventions), Sub-pattern 5 audit-both-ends for any new aggregation queries. **Sprint 53+ post-volume.** Requires meaningful tender volume (50+ tenders per week minimum) to produce statistically-useful signal — defer until BKN-onward operational baseline established.

156. ~~**Carrier route RSC payload regression.**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-17 in v3.8.abx** (Sprint 52.hotfix.a) — **then REOPENED in v3.8.aby** (Sprint 52.hotfix.a.b rollback per Item 157). The explicit `.html` rewrites resolved the Gmail iOS RSC payload issue but surfaced a latent redirect loop on `/carrier/dashboard` (ERR_TOO_MANY_REDIRECTS post-login). Rollback prioritized known-working state; combined fix queued for Sprint 52.hotfix.c after redirect-loop diagnosis. Pre-fix root cause notes preserved: `_redirects` rule `/carrier/* /carrier/:splat 200` echoes `:splat` as identity rewrite target; Cloudflare Pages resolves the extensionless path ambiguously between `out/carrier/<name>.html` and `out/carrier/<name>.txt` siblings (Next.js static export generates both). Gmail iOS WebView Accept-header content negotiation lands on the `.txt` RSC payload. **Status: OPEN (Sprint 52.hotfix.c candidate, combined fix with Item 157).**

157. ~~**Sprint 52.hotfix.a rollback — /carrier/dashboard ERR_TOO_MANY_REDIRECTS.**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-17 in v3.8.aby** (Sprint 52.hotfix.a.b). Sprint 52.hotfix.a replaced the `/carrier/* /carrier/:splat 200` catch-all with 5 explicit `.html` rewrites for Next.js carrier routes. Production post-deploy verification surfaced a latent redirect loop: INTEGRITY EXPRESS carrier completed login successfully then `/carrier/dashboard` returned ERR_TOO_MANY_REDIRECTS. The redirect loop is presumed to be in the carrier dashboard's auth gate (client-side useCarrierAuth hook OR layout-level redirect), interacting with the new `.html` explicit rewrite in a way the `:splat` echo didn't surface. **Rollback fix:** reverted `_redirects` line 22 to the original `/carrier/* /carrier/:splat 200`. Restores known-working /carrier/dashboard behavior at the cost of reintroducing the Gmail iOS RSC payload regression (Item 156 re-opened). Combined fix planned for Sprint 52.hotfix.c after Phase A diagnostic on BOTH issues — likely involves either (a) auditing the carrier dashboard auth-redirect path for the loop trigger, (b) adopting a hybrid `_redirects` pattern that adds `.html` rewrite for /carrier/login + /carrier/forgot-password + /carrier/reset-password (where the RSC issue surfaced) while leaving `/carrier/dashboard/*` under the `:splat` echo until the auth loop is diagnosed, OR (c) deeper Next.js static export config / middleware investigation.

158. **Parallel carrier status-update endpoints consolidation.** Surfaced 2026-05-17 during Sprint 52.hotfix.c Phase A audit. Two parallel carrier-side status-update routes exist in the codebase: (a) `POST /api/carrier-loads/:id/status` at [`carrierLoads.ts:341`](backend/src/routes/carrierLoads.ts#L341) — what the carrier portal `/my-loads` page actually calls (controller inline, no auditLog wrapper, no central transition validator); (b) `PATCH /api/loads/:id/carrier-status` at [`loads.ts:39`](backend/src/routes/loads.ts#L39) — separate controller `carrierUpdateStatus`, separate validator `updateLoadStatusSchema`, `auditLog("UPDATE_STATUS", "Load")` wrapper. Both gate on `authorize("CARRIER")`. Frontend calls only endpoint (a); endpoint (b) is dead surface with no frontend caller. Same parallel-endpoints class as Sprint 52.hotfix.b Item 156 diagnostic (`/carrier-tenders/active` vs `/api/carrier/tenders`). **Sprint shape:** consolidate to one endpoint; recommend keeping the PATCH variant in loads.ts (auditLog wrapper, REST-correct HTTP verb, validator already separated) and migrating the carrier portal call site. ~30-50 LOC across 3 files (loads.ts unchanged, carrierLoads.ts:335-409 deleted, frontend my-loads page mutation URL + method updated). **Sprint 53+ candidate** — not BKN-blocking; current endpoint A works, just structurally redundant.

159. **Central LoadStatus state-machine validator.** Surfaced 2026-05-17 during Sprint 52.hotfix.c Phase A audit. 13+ distinct write sites mutate `Load.status` across the codebase (tenderController × 4, loadController × 5, carrierLoads.ts, loads.ts/carrierUpdateStatus, documentController, checkCallController, customerController, rateConfirmationController) with NO central transition rules. Each write site accepts whatever status its caller specifies. The `LoadStatus` enum has 18 values across the lifecycle pipeline (DRAFT → POSTED → TENDERED → BOOKED → DISPATCHED → AT_PICKUP → LOADED → IN_TRANSIT → AT_DELIVERY → DELIVERED → POD_RECEIVED → INVOICED → COMPLETED + TONU/CANCELLED/PICKED_UP legacy alias); CLAUDE.md §A.1 documents the canonical state machine but it lives in docs, not code. Carrier portal frontend has a `statusTransitions` map at [`my-loads/page.tsx:12-19`](frontend/src/app/carrier/dashboard/my-loads/page.tsx#L12) that enforces transitions client-side only — backend accepts any of 5 enum values regardless of current status. **Sprint shape:** central `validateLoadStatusTransition(from, to, actor)` helper at `backend/src/lib/loadStateMachine.ts` returning `{ allowed: boolean, reason?: string }`; refactor 13 write sites to invoke validator before `prisma.load.update`; auditLog rejected transitions. ~150-250 LOC across 1 new file + 8 callers (some controllers have multiple write sites). **Sprint 53+ multi-day epic** — significant refactor; gates on Sprint 52 epic completion. Methodology benefit: backend becomes authoritative on transition legality, frontend `statusTransitions` map becomes UI-hint only (not the only enforcement).

160. **ShipmentStatus ↔ LoadStatus enum gap.** Surfaced 2026-05-17 during Sprint 52.hotfix.c Phase A audit. `enum ShipmentStatus` (schema.prisma:197-206) has 8 values: PENDING, BOOKED, DISPATCHED, PICKED_UP, IN_TRANSIT, DELIVERED, COMPLETED, CANCELLED. `enum LoadStatus` (schema.prisma:26-45) has 18 values including the carrier-side states the ShipmentStatus enum LACKS: AT_PICKUP, LOADED, AT_DELIVERY, POD_RECEIVED, INVOICED, TONU. acceptTender at [`tenderController.ts:106`](backend/src/controllers/tenderController.ts#L106) auto-creates a Shipment with `status: "BOOKED"` (line 110) — that value DOES exist in both enums. But if any future flow reads Load.status and writes that value to Shipment.status, the 6 LoadStatus values absent from ShipmentStatus would fail Prisma validation. **Risk profile:** latent — no current code path writes LoadStatus values directly to Shipment.status (acceptTender hardcodes "BOOKED"); future refactor or feature add could trip this gap. **Sprint shape:** decide canonical: (α) expand ShipmentStatus to mirror full LoadStatus pipeline (Shipment becomes a status-tracking projection of Load), (β) keep ShipmentStatus narrow as billing/financial-cycle states only and document that Load.status is the operational source of truth, (γ) drop the Shipment model entirely if it's redundant with Load. Pairs naturally with Item 159 (central state machine) — the enum gap is the data-side expression of the same architectural ambiguity. **Sprint 53+ architectural decision sprint** — requires product call on what Shipment.status represents semantically.

161. **REOPENED + CLOSED 2026-05-17 in v3.8.aca (Sprint 53) — Auth cookie isolation. Original "no bug" close was premature. Sprint 53.a (v3.8.acb) hotfix follow-up — substring-match prefix collision.** Sprint 53 shipped with a substring `.includes("/carrier")` match in `resolveCookieToken` at `middleware/auth.ts:90` that wrongly routed AE-side endpoints with "carrier" in the name to the carrier cookie. Wasi's post-deploy smoke surfaced 403 on `GET /api/carriers` — same architectural class as Sprint 53's parent bug (substring vs proper prefix matching), just at a different layer. **V2 audit** during the Sprint 53.a hotfix enumerated `/api/carrier` (singular) as a genuine audience-mixed mount (6 carrier-facing endpoints `dashboard|scorecard|revenue|bonuses|onboarding-status|documents` lacking explicit `authorize("CARRIER")` + 6 AE-side endpoints `all|:id/detail|:id|verify/:id|admin-setup|capacity-feed` with explicit `authorize("ADMIN", "CEO", ...)`). Single-axis allow-list can't resolve both audiences without one side breaking in the dual-portal scenario. **Decision locked Option B per Wasi 2026-05-17:** allow-list EXCLUDES `/api/carrier` (singular) — the 6 carrier-facing endpoints under it return AE-scoped data when both portals are logged in same browser. Real-world users hold one role per browser so the fallback chain rescues; only deploy-test scenarios hit this. Architectural fix (split mount to move 6 AE-side endpoints into existing `/api/carriers` plural which has overlapping `getAllCarriers` controller anyway, OR introduce X-Portal request header from frontend) tracked as **Sprint 54+ candidate** — same priority as Item 158 (parallel-endpoint consolidation), same class. **Sprint 53.a fix shape:** explicit `CARRIER_PORTAL_MOUNTS` array (`/api/carrier-auth`, `/api/carrier-loads`, `/api/carrier-compliance`, `/api/carrier-payments`, `/api/carrier-tenders`) + `SHIPPER_PORTAL_MOUNTS` array (`/api/shipper-portal`) + new `matchesPortalMount(baseUrl, mounts)` helper using `baseUrl === p || baseUrl.startsWith(p + "/")`. ~25 LOC net change in single file. **Sub-pattern observation gains a second fire:** Sprint 52.hotfix.c missed the cookie layer entirely (Sprint 53 fire #1); Sprint 53 missed the substring-vs-prefix distinction within the cookie layer (fire #2 — same root cause class, one level deeper). The methodology principle banked at Item 161's first close ("Phase A on auth/permission symptoms must reach the storage/transport layer") needs an extension: *"and the prefix-vs-substring distinction within transport-layer routing logic is a hot edge — verify by enumerating ALL mount paths containing the keyword, not by trusting heuristic boundary matching."* Two fires; one more from a future independent incident promotes the principle to §19 canonical per sub-rule c three-fire convention. Sprint 53.a closes 53's regression; original Sprint 53 closure of items 9/10/11/14 remains in force.

 Sprint 52.hotfix.c attributed the carrier "Insufficient permissions" + three-surface status divergence to *observer-identity-confusion* (operator with multi-role privileges polluting their own test session). **Corrected RCA:** all three portals (AE Console, Carrier Portal, Shipper Portal) shared a single httpOnly cookie name `srl_token` set by `backend/src/utils/cookies.ts:14`. Same browser logging into two roles overwrote the cookie — second login replaced the first's JWT. `authorize("CARRIER")` at `backend/src/middleware/auth.ts:165` fired "Insufficient permissions" when the carrier-portal call ran with the ADMIN JWT that had just overwritten the carrier one. The system_log entries Sprint 52.hotfix.c surfaced (`whaider@silkroutelogistics.ai` denied on carrier endpoints) were the contamination *trail*, not test apparatus error. The "test from incognito" workaround masked the bug because incognito has no other portal's cookie to overwrite the carrier one. **Fix shipped Sprint 53:** per-portal cookie names (`srl_token_ae` / `srl_token_carrier` / `srl_token_shipper`), middleware picks the right cookie by `req.baseUrl` prefix, role passed to `setTokenCookie(res, token, role)` at all 14 callsites (authController.ts × 7, routes/auth.ts × 2, carrierAuth.ts × 5), legacy `srl_token` read as one-deploy migration fallback and cleared on next logout. Closes user punch-list items 9 (mark-delivered "Insufficient permissions"), 10 (carrier account auto-switched mid-test), 11 (carrier signout logged out AE). Bundled with Item 14 closure (loginLimiter bumped 5→20 in routes/auth.ts + routes/carrierAuth.ts, authLimiter bumped 30→100 in server.ts — Wasi's lockout during the lifecycle test). **Methodology observation banked as sub-pattern candidate (awaits 3-fire validation per §19 canonical promotion convention):** *"Phase A on auth/permission symptoms must reach the storage/transport layer (cookies, sessions, tokens, headers), not stop at the role gate."* Sprint 52.hotfix.c's Phase A inspected User.role bytes, system_logs, and Neon DB state — but stopped before the cookie layer that delivered the JWT. The "observer-identity-confusion" interpretation was internally consistent with what Phase A surfaced; the gap was scope, not reasoning. Extends Sub-pattern 5 (audit-both-ends-of-data-flow) from data flow to transport flow. Fire #1 banked here. Original "no bug" close preserved below for history.

161-original. ~~**Sprint 52.hotfix.c closed — no bug (observer-identity confusion fire #1).**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-17 (chore, no version bump, no code change).** Reported symptom was carrier "Update Status: AT PICKUP" button returning "Insufficient permissions" + three-surface status divergence across carrier portal / AE Load Board row / AE Load Board detail panel. Phase A R1-R5 audit + Wasi-side Neon verification confirmed system working as designed: User.role = "CARRIER" byte-exact (length 7, hex `43415252494552`), system_logs healthy (65 SECURITY warnings in past 7 days, latest write <1 minute old at audit time), all recent `authorize()` denials attributed to `whaider@silkroutelogistics.ai` (ADMIN role) attempting carrier-portal endpoints — those denials were CORRECT per the role gate. INTEGRITY EXPRESS session itself was never the denied actor; the symptom surfaced from **cross-role cache contamination from admin's testing session** (admin had AE token in browser storage while testing carrier flows in same tab/window). The three-surface status divergence dissolved when the test was re-run from an incognito window with carrier credentials only — confirming the divergence was browser-state pollution, not data drift. **Methodology observation (fire #1):** *observer-identity-confusion antipattern* — when an operator with multi-role privileges tests a role-restricted flow without isolating session context, observed "bug" may be the test apparatus, not the system. Mitigation: always test role-restricted flows from incognito or separate browser profile with test-subject credentials only. Worth banking for second/third fire validation before promoting to §19 canonical (parallel to sub-pattern 13 + sub-pattern 15 three-fire lineage convention). Sprint 52.hotfix.c closes with zero source change, zero data fix; the Phase A audit work IS the deliverable — Items 158/159/160 banked as collateral findings.

162. **Track & Trace drawer ROUTE visualization regression** (originally directed as "Item 161" — directive was stale by one commit; Item 161 had just been consumed by Sprint 52.hotfix.c no-bug close in commit `a2c0e12`; renumbered to 162 per sub-pattern 6 concurrent-sprint-coordination correction). Banked 2026-05-17. **Class:** UI regression + sub-pattern 5 (audit-both-ends-of-data-flow — data populated server-side, not consumed client-side). **Severity:** P2 (operational hygiene, not load-blocking). **Surfaced on L7492033667 at POD_RECEIVED + INVOICED stages.** Symptoms: (1) Route bar shows static colored segment + dotted tail with no truck position marker. (2) "Current position" field renders em-dash despite the GPS panel below it showing `Source: AE_MANUAL`, last ping `May 17 10:22 AM`. (3) "ETA" field empty. (4) "Internal server error" banner visible on INVOICED stage drawer — possibly the ETA compute endpoint failing, adjacent issue worth isolating during Phase A. **Expected behavior:** (a) truck icon positioned proportionally along the route based on last known location point; (b) Current position populated from same source as GPS panel; (c) ETA computed from remaining distance + average speed or carrier ETA pings; (d) source provenance shown on the route visualization itself via badge/label — `AE_MANUAL` → "Last update: phone call", `EDI_214` → "Last update: carrier EDI ping", `ELD_GPS` → "Last update: device GPS", `CARRIER_CHECKIN` → "Last update: carrier portal", `GEOFENCE` → "Last update: geofence trigger"; (e) timestamp on the route bar, not buried in the GPS panel below. **Files likely involved (Phase A to confirm):** `frontend/src/components/tracking/TrackingDrawer.tsx` or similar; `frontend/src/components/tracking/RouteVisualization.tsx` or similar; backend endpoint serving the drawer — likely `GET /api/loads/:id/tracking` or `/track-trace/:id` namespace; may share data source with the GPS panel — if so, regression is in the route component only (consumer-side bug). **Sprint shape:** Phase A audit to identify which component owns the route bar render + which endpoint feeds it; cross-reference against GPS panel data source to confirm sub-pattern 5 class (data populated, consumer doesn't read). Likely small fix (~30-50 LOC) if regression is purely consumer-side; ~80-120 LOC if ETA compute endpoint also needs hardening. **Related:** Item 159 (Load.status state machine — same write-many-no-validation class as the GPS source field), sub-pattern 5 (audit-both-ends-of-data-flow). **Sprint timing:** post-Sprint-52 epic completion, or interleaved if it surfaces operational friction on the BKN onboarding walkthrough.

180. **Order Builder polish cluster — 11 small UX/operational fixes (umbrella).** Banked 2026-05-20 from Wasi's Sprint 59.c walk-through Q&A. Each sub-item is small (10-80 LOC), single-commit eligible, and not BKN-blocking on its own. Banked as an umbrella so they can be sequenced together when the polish budget opens. None depend on each other; can ship in any order.

   **180.1 — "Duplicate this order" action.** AE running repeat lanes (e.g. weekly BKN Detroit → Chicago) re-keys 30+ fields per draft. Add a one-click clone button on the drafts banner card + per-order kebab menu on the drafts list (Item 179) that creates a new draft with all fields except `id`, `orderNumber`, `loadId`, `status` copied from the source. ~30 LOC.

   **180.2 — Save-as-template for recurring lanes.** Different from 180.1 (template is named + reusable indefinitely; clone is one-shot). Schema addition: new `OrderTemplate` model with `customerId`, `name`, `formData` JSON. New `Template` selector in Section 1 of Order Builder beside Customer picker. AE picks "BKN — Detroit→Chicago weekly" → form prefills from template. Save current draft as new template via "Save as template…" action. ~120-180 LOC + 1 migration.

   **180.3 — Three text-field confusion (specialInstructions / driverInstructions / internalNotes).** Three textareas stacked vertically with similar UI invite AE error (carrier-sensitive info typed into wrong field, or AE-only context where carrier will see it). Single textarea with "visible to" radio (Carrier on rate-con / Driver on rate-con / Internal only) would be cleaner. Backend keeps the 3 columns; frontend collapses to one input + a visibility selector that writes to the corresponding field. ~50 LOC frontend.

   **180.4 — Customer-facing quote approve magic link.** Send quote today emails the customer with the price; customer replies by email; AE manually flips `Order.status = "quote_approved"` (or skips entirely). Add a signed token in the quote email body → public `/quote/approve/<token>` page → customer clicks "Approve at $X,XXX" → backend verifies token + sets `status = "quote_approved"` + emails AE confirmation. Same JWT shape as the magic-link tender accept proposed for Sprint 52b (Item 142). Tightens the quote loop. ~80-120 LOC.

   **180.5 — Quote preview before send.** AE can't see what customer will see before clicking Send quote — risk of typo/rate-error reaching the inbox. Add "Preview email" modal that renders the actual email HTML (calling the same builder used by `sendQuote` controller). Same modal pattern as the RC PDF preview. ~50 LOC.

   **180.6 — Accessorial picker with per-customer negotiated rates.** Current accessorial entry is type + amount + payer (free-form). No connection to customer contract rates. When AE picks "Detention" for BKN, should auto-fill $50/hr (BKN's negotiated rate) vs Acme's $75/hr. Backend has `customer.contractRates` JSON or similar (verify in Phase A). Frontend reads customer's accessorial rates on customer-select and offers them as picker options. ~60-100 LOC.

   **180.7 — Margin-floor alert in OrderSidebar.** OrderSidebar surfaces margin % in real-time. Doesn't appear to alert when target cost produces margin below a configured floor. Add red warning chip when `margin < settings.minMarginPercent` (per-customer override possible). Settings live in `settings` page or `customer.minMarginPercent` column. ~30-50 LOC + maybe 1 schema field.

   **180.8 — `?resume=<orderId>` URL deep-link.** Item 179's drafts page needs URL-shareable resume paths. Today the drafts banner uses internal state mutation (`resumeDraft(d.id)`) with no URL change — AE can't paste a draft link into Slack/email. Add `useEffect` reading `searchParams.get("resume")` on mount; if present, fire `resumeDraft(orderId)`. ~10 LOC. Pairs with Item 179.

   **180.9 — Autosave indicator mirrored near footer CTAs.** Sprint 59.c kept DraftStatus in top header. AE working at the bottom of the form doesn't see it while clicking Tender/Waterfall/Load Board/DAT. Mirror a smaller `<DraftStatus>` chip inside the new footer button row (left side, before the dispatch buttons). ~5 LOC.

   **180.10 — Dispatch error banner relocated to footer.** Sprint 59.b's dispatch error banner renders after the top header but BEFORE the form columns. When dispatch fails from the footer Sprint 59.c moved them to, AE has to scroll back to the top to see the error. Move the banner to be a sibling of the footer button row (rendered above the buttons when isError, below when at very bottom of form). ~10 LOC re-parent.

   **180.11 — Origin/Destination facility name + address visual hierarchy.** Today Section 1 (Origin) + Section 2 (Destination) display fields flat — facility-picker result and address inputs all render at the same visual weight. Wasi 2026-05-20: facility NAME should be the prominent label at the top of each section ("QCC Distribution Center" in larger/bolder type), then address ("1234 Industrial Pkwy, San Diego, CA 92154") as secondary text below. Mirrors the canonical "name primary, supporting metadata below" pattern from CRM customer detail + Carrier Engagement Drawer's selected-carrier card ([CarrierEngagementDrawer.tsx:608-628](frontend/src/components/drawer/CarrierEngagementDrawer.tsx#L608-L628) for reference shape). Apply to both origin + destination sections. Address fields stay editable for AE override when facility lookup misses or a one-off address is needed. ~40-60 LOC across both sections (FacilityPicker result rendering + section header restructure).

   **Sprint slot:** post-Sprint-59.c soak, queue alongside Item 179 (drafts surface) + Item 178 (multi-line freight edit) as the Order Builder polish cluster. Sub-items can ship as a single bundled sprint OR as 11 individual atomic commits depending on operational urgency. 178. **Multi-line freight edit UI in Carrier Engagement Drawer.** Banked 2026-05-18 alongside Sprint 59.b (v3.8.act) closure. Sprint 59.b ships single-line freight edit in the drawer (primary line from `OrderForm.lineItems[0]` → drawer's pieces/packageType/weight/description fields) plus a "+N more lines" read-only chip when the Order Builder draft has `lineItems.length > 1`. Extra lines (2..N) round-trip through the drawer's `lineItemsRest` prop unchanged and merge back into the `lineItems[]` array on POST `/api/loads/with-tender` submit, so multi-line BOL rendering is preserved without loss. **What's missing:** in-drawer multi-line EDIT UI (table view, add/remove/reorder rows, per-line hazmat fields). AE who needs to edit line 2+ post-Order-Builder has to either (a) cancel the tender, edit in Order Builder, re-open drawer, OR (b) edit the load post-creation via the EditLoadModal (Item 3 backlog, also pending). **Sprint shape:** widen drawer Freight section to a small editable table when `lineItemsRest.length > 0` — re-uses the LineItemsSection component from `frontend/src/components/orders/LineItemsSection.tsx` (already extracted) or adapts it for the drawer's cream surface. ~80-120 LOC. Pairs naturally with Sprint 60 Mode 2 (review existing load) since Mode 2 also needs multi-line edit. **Sprint slot:** Sprint 60 candidate alongside Mode 2 scope.

177. **Visual-verification protocol gate — mandatory for drawer/modal/canvas-rendering sprints.** Banked 2026-05-18 alongside Sprint 59.a (v3.8.acn) hotfix closure. **Codified per Wasi ratification 2026-05-18.** Pre-Sprint-59.a state: pre-commit gates were `tsc --noEmit` + `next build` (Sub-pattern 11 CI-parity canonical). Sprint 59 shipped with both gates green but missed 4 user-facing UX bugs (horizontal tabs vs vertical IconTabs canonical, empty form on open, carrier name mismatch, customer rate duplication) — all compile-time clean, none caught by tsc or build. **Sub-pattern 8 (conditional-render-visual-verification) fired again** — second instance in this session arc (first was Sprint 48.c signature overlap at Item 139 canonical). Protocol mandate: **any sprint that ships a new drawer, modal, canvas-rendered surface, or visual layout restructure MUST include a pre-push visual smoke** — either via Playwright headed-browser screenshot (when CI-feasible) OR explicit Phase A code-trace of the visual class structure against the canonical reference, NOT just function signatures. Sub-pattern 8 sub-rule a: *"code-trace must include the visual-outcome class chain, not just the call graph."* Sub-pattern 8 sub-rule b: *"every new drawer surface re-verifies against the canonical right-drawer reference (currently T&T LoadDetailDrawer at [LoadDetailDrawer.tsx:108-112](frontend/src/app/dashboard/track-trace/LoadDetailDrawer.tsx#L108)) — IconTabs left strip + flex-1 main content sibling — NOT inline horizontal tabs in the form body."* Future Phase A audits checking drawer canonical must trace BOTH the component file's tab pattern (already done at Sprint 59 A3) AND the wrapping flex direction (`flex` vs `flex-col`) AND the sibling structure (`<IconTabs />` as first child, then `<div className="flex-1 flex flex-col min-w-0">`). Single-axis component-file audit produced the Sprint 59 miss. **Sprint shape for future drawer work:** Phase A canonical-trace adds step "A_visual" — read the canonical drawer's outermost JSX wrapper class chain + first 3 child siblings, document the visual hierarchy in the report, and confirm Phase B implementation matches. Costs ~10 minutes per Phase A; saves the kind of post-deploy hotfix that Sprint 59.a was. Item 177 closes structurally — the protocol is canonical from this commit forward, not a pending implementation. Pairs with Sub-pattern 11 (CI-parity) — together they form a two-gate pre-push discipline (compile gate + visual gate) for any UX-shipping sprint.

Net: AE thought they'd tendered the load to a carrier; carrier received nothing; load sat at status POSTED with stale directTenderCarrierId metadata. **Sub-rule c authoritative-source verification (Sprint 59 Phase A):** quoted [orders/page.tsx:408-437 pre-Sprint-59] (createLoad mutation POSTs empty body to `/orders/:id/convert-to-load`) + [routes/orders.ts:516-524 pre-Sprint-59] (no `direct_tender` branch in dispatch routing) — confirming the silent failure mechanism. **Closure path: structural deletion, not patch.** Sprint 59 deleted the radios + DirectTenderPicker + createLoad mutation + convert-to-load backend handler entirely. The user can no longer select "direct_tender" without going through the Carrier Engagement Drawer which atomically creates Load + Tender + RC via `POST /api/loads/with-tender`. No silent-failure surface to maintain. See Item 176 above for full Sprint 59 details.

175. **RSC payload 404 on root `/index.txt?_rsc=*` requests.** Banked 2026-05-18 during Sprint 174.a (v3.8.ach) hotfix audit. Symptom in Wasi's DevTools console: `/index.txt?_rsc=1ri1u: Failed to load resource: the server responded with a status of 404`. Same architectural class as §13.3 Item 156 (carrier route RSC payload — Gmail iOS WebView Accept-header content negotiation) but on the root path rather than `/carrier/*`. Cloudflare Pages doesn't have an `/index.txt` static file because Next.js static export generates `/index.html` only; the `?_rsc=*` query string is a Next.js App Router internal RSC (React Server Components) payload fetch attempt. Static export shouldn't be emitting RSC fetches at all, but framework versions occasionally regress on this. **Sprint shape:** investigate which component or framework version is emitting the RSC fetch. Options: (a) check `frontend/next.config.ts` for any RSC-enabling config that conflicts with `output: "export"`; (b) audit framework version + Next.js patch notes for RSC-in-static-export regressions; (c) add `_redirects` rule `/index.txt /index.html 200` as a band-aid that satisfies the fetch with the actual page content. Low priority — RSC payload fetch failures don't break the page render (Next.js gracefully falls back to client-side navigation), they just produce console noise. Pairs with Item 156 architecturally (same RSC content-negotiation class). Sprint slot: post-BKN cleanup unless a user-facing symptom surfaces.

174. ~~**Shipper login role-gate gap — carrier creds work on /shipper/login.**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-18 in v3.8.acf** (Sprint Item 174, Option β+γ+α defense-in-depth). Symptom: INTEGRITY EXPRESS (aliabbas6361@gmail.com, role=CARRIER) could complete /shipper/login → OTP → land on /shipper/dashboard authenticated, despite being a carrier account. Shipper API gates (`authorize("SHIPPER")`) held so no data leak, but portal-boundary integrity violated. **Three-layer gap audited:** (a) shipper login page reuses AE auth endpoints — [shipper/login/page.tsx:10,46](frontend/src/app/shipper/login/page.tsx#L10) imports `useAuthStore` calling `/api/auth/login` + `/api/auth/verify-otp` (the AE endpoints, not separate shipper paths); (b) `/api/auth/login` at [authController.ts:148-218](backend/src/controllers/authController.ts#L148) had no role gate — only password + lockout + isActive checks; (c) `/api/auth/verify-otp` had SHIPPER-specific `checkShipperApproval` but no refusal for non-SHIPPER roles — carrier flowed straight through to JWT issuance; (d) shipper dashboard layout at [shipper/dashboard/layout.tsx:48-61](frontend/src/app/shipper/dashboard/layout.tsx#L48) had no role check — only `if (!currentUser)`. **Fix shape — defense-in-depth at three layers (Option β+γ+α combined):** Layer γ-1 backend validator: optional `expectedRole: "AE" | "SHIPPER"` added to `loginSchema` ([validators/auth.ts](backend/src/validators/auth.ts)) + `otpSchema` ([routes/auth.ts:23](backend/src/routes/auth.ts#L23)). Layer γ-2 backend controller: new `AE_ROLES` set + `rolesMatch(userRole, expectedRole)` helper at [authController.ts:21-30](backend/src/controllers/authController.ts#L21); role check in `login` after isActive check + in `handleVerifyOtp` after user lookup. 401 + `code: "ROLE_MISMATCH"`, message "Invalid credentials for this portal." Layer γ-3 useAuthStore: `login` + `verifyOtp` signatures extended with optional `expectedRole`, body conditionally includes the field. Layer β shipper login: passes `"SHIPPER"` to both calls; post-OTP frontend role check (defense-in-depth in case backend gate fails) — on mismatch calls `/api/auth/logout` + `useAuthStore.getState().clearAuth()` + shows error. Layer γ-4 AE login: passes `"AE"` in both fetch bodies (page uses raw fetch, not useAuthStore). Layer α shipper dashboard layout: `bounceIfWrongRole` helper called from both fresh-load and cached-user branches — on mismatch calls `/api/auth/logout` + clearAuth + `router.replace("/shipper/login")`. **Carrier portal unaffected** — uses `/api/carrier-auth/*` which already gates strictly to CARRIER role per [carrierAuth.ts:70](backend/src/routes/carrierAuth.ts#L70) + [carrierAuth.ts:153](backend/src/routes/carrierAuth.ts#L153). **Methodology — sub-pattern fire #1 banked: "portal-boundary-defense-asymmetry":** *"When one portal (carrier) has rigorous role gating across login/OTP/layout but another (shipper) reuses shared AE auth endpoints without role gates, the asymmetry becomes a portal-boundary violation surface. Audit all three portals' login flows for symmetric defense at each layer."* Sub-pattern awaits fire #2 + #3 from independent incidents before §19 canonical promotion. Pairs with Item 168 (audit-wrong-code-path) and Item 169 (interceptor-without-context-awareness) — three consecutive scope/context-discipline sub-pattern candidates banked in the Sprint 53→54→174 arc.

Phase A misread context and audited `backend/src/controllers/authController.ts` ADMIN TOTP flow (`handleVerifyOtp` + `handleTotpLoginVerify`) — the AE-portal code path. Wasi corrected: he was testing the **CARRIER** portal flow, not AE. Carrier auth lives at `backend/src/routes/carrierAuth.ts` with its own `handleVerifyOtp` and totp-verify handlers, separate `useCarrierAuth` Zustand store, separate `/carrier/login` UI. Sprint 54 dropped Item 11 from its atomic scope; re-audit scheduled for next session against the actual carrier code path. **Sprint shape for re-audit:** (1) read `backend/src/routes/carrierAuth.ts` OTP verify + TOTP verify handlers verbatim, focus on the setTokenCookie call site + which role string is passed; (2) read `frontend/src/hooks/useCarrierAuth.ts` post-verify state setter + redirect logic; (3) read `frontend/src/app/carrier/dashboard/layout.tsx` AuthGuard equivalent that fires loadUser → /api/carrier-auth/me; (4) reproduce in incognito on prod with DevTools Network preserve-log, capture the 401 response body + Cookie request header on the failing endpoint after carrier OTP success; (5) cross-reference against Sprint 53.a CARRIER_PORTAL_MOUNTS allow-list to confirm `/api/carrier-auth/me` baseUrl correctly matches `/api/carrier-auth` and reads srl_token_carrier cookie. **Methodology lesson (banked as Sub-rule c sub-pattern candidate fire #1 — "audit-wrong-code-path"):** *"When user reports symptom in flow X, Phase A must verify it's auditing flow X's actual code path before deep-diving."* The OTP login audit looked at admin TOTP verify because the AE flow was the default mental model; the user's report was carrier flow. Sub-pattern banks alongside Sprint 53 + 53.a fires #1 (cookie layer scope) + #2 (substring-vs-prefix within cookie layer); cumulative pattern: Phase A scope-discipline failures cluster around "what was the user actually testing?" rather than "where does the code think it lives?". Sub-pattern awaits fire #2 + #3 from independent incidents before §19 canonical promotion per sub-rule c three-fire convention.

169. **HTTP interceptor-without-context-awareness (sub-pattern candidate fire #1).** Banked 2026-05-17 alongside Sprint 54 close of Item 6 (View Tender CTA wrong portal). The frontend axios 401 interceptor at `frontend/src/lib/api.ts:35-42` (pre-Sprint-54) made a portal-routing decision (`/auth/login` redirect target) based only on the response status code, with no reference to `window.location.pathname` to know which portal the request originated from. Net effect: a logged-out carrier landing on `/carrier/dashboard/tenders` from an email CTA got bounced to the AE login page on first 401, despite the carrier portal having its own `/carrier/login` surface. Sprint 54 fixed by reading `window.location.pathname` and picking `/carrier/login` / `/shipper/login` / `/auth/login` accordingly. **Methodology lesson banked as Sub-rule c sub-pattern candidate fire #1 — "interceptor-without-context-awareness":** *"Frontend HTTP interceptors that make routing decisions on responses (e.g. 401 → redirect) must read request context (URL path, expected portal) before deciding the target. Hardcoded fallbacks erase user origin context."* Candidate awaits fire #2 + #3 from independent incidents before §19 canonical promotion. Pairs with Items 168 + Sprint 53 audit-wrong-code-path lineage — both point to the same broader meta-pattern: scope/context discipline in audit AND in code design. **Cross-reference:** Item 168 (audit-wrong-code-path, methodology); this Item 169 (interceptor-without-context, code-design). Different layers, same shape.

170. **Carrier portal Rate Confirmation download visibility (Sprint Phase 2 follow-on).** Banked 2026-05-17 alongside Sprint Phase 2 close (auto-RC on tender accept, v3.8.acd). Phase 2 produces auto-DRAFT RCs on tender accept and AE manually sends them via existing `POST /api/rate-confirmations/:id/send` (email + PDF attachment to carrier). What's STILL missing: a carrier-portal endpoint that exposes RC download by loadId — `GET /api/rate-confirmations/:id/pdf` is CARRIER-authorized but requires the RC's UUID which the carrier doesn't have. `GET /api/rate-confirmations/load/:loadId` lookup is AE-only (carrier role not in authorize list at `backend/src/routes/rateConfirmations.ts:20`). **Sprint shape:** (a) new endpoint `GET /api/rate-confirmations/load/:loadId/latest/pdf` (CARRIER authorized, verifies carrier owns the load, looks up most recent RC, streams PDF via existing `generateEnhancedRateConfirmation`) — returns 404 if no RC exists yet; (b) add CARRIER to `GET /api/rate-confirmations/load/:loadId` authorize list for metadata reads (status, sentAt, signed flag) so the carrier UI can gate the download button correctly; (c) frontend `/carrier/dashboard/my-loads` load detail panel — replace `rateConfirmationPdfUrl` column gating with TanStack query against the new endpoint, "Download Rate Confirmation" button always visible for BOOKED+ status with disabled "pending" state when no RC exists. ~50 LOC across 2 files backend + 1 file frontend. **Priority:** queue after Phase 2 deploy soak — carriers currently receive RC via email attachment so Phase 2 is functionally complete without this; portal download is a re-download convenience. Pairs with Item 171 (auto-send) — if 171 ships first, this becomes more relevant. **Sprint slot:** post-Sprint-54 carrier-OTP audit (Item 168), interleave before Sprint 56 if BKN onboarding asks for re-download UX.

171. **Auto-send the RC on tender accept (Sprint Phase 2.b follow-on).** Banked 2026-05-17 alongside Sprint Phase 2 close. Phase 2 shipped Option α (auto-DRAFT + AE manual review + send) per the locked decision; the alternative Option β (auto-DRAFT + auto-SEND) was deferred until the auto-fill mapping proves correct against real test loads. **Sprint shape:** add an env-gated or per-customer flag (e.g., `Customer.autoSendRateConfirmation: Boolean`) that, when true, fires the existing `POST /api/rate-confirmations/:id/send` immediately after the auto-RC is created. AE still gets the notification with deep-link, but the RC is also already in the carrier's inbox within seconds of accept. **Risks:** wrong-data RC in carrier's inbox is recoverable (AE re-sends after fix) but damages trust on early loads. **Trigger conditions for elevation:** auto-fill mapping has been smoke-verified over at least 3 real test loads with no field corrections needed; BKN onboarding asks for industry-standard auto-send timing. ~30 LOC: per-customer or env-gate read inside acceptTender + acceptTenderOnBehalf, fires `sendRateConfirmation` controller's internals after auto-RC create.

**Authority-age compliance epic — logged 2026-05-21 (Wasi cross-cutting directive, v3.8.ahj-ahn):**

182. **Authority-age compliance epic (v3.8.ahj → v3.8.ahn).** Surfaced 2026-05-21 from Wasi cross-cutting directive: carriers whose FMCSA operating authority is younger than 18 months are HARD-BLOCKED from hauling SRL loads. Override window exists for authority age 12-18 months, accessible to ADMIN+CEO via the existing Sprint 40 ComplianceOverride flow (24h expiry + 15/30-day quota unchanged). Authority age under 12 months is hard-block with no override. Authority age 18+ months auto-allows.

    **Locked decisions (do not re-litigate per Item 182 epic directive):**
    - **Threshold (Option A):** age <12 mo → hard-block; age 12-18 mo → override-eligible (ADMIN/CEO); age ≥18 mo → auto-allow.
    - **Override mechanism:** reuse existing `ComplianceOverride` table from Sprint 40 / Item 58 with reason text encoding "authority-age-override" semantics. No new override model — keeps the audit + quota infrastructure single-sourced.
    - **Override role:** ADMIN+CEO (same gating as Sprint 40 compliance override).
    - **Override expiry + quota:** 24 hours + 15-per-30-days per carrier, unchanged from Sprint 40 defaults.
    - **Existing APPROVED carrier grandfathering (Option γ):** soft-grandfather. Carriers already APPROVED at the time v3.8.ahl ships are flagged with an AE warning on tender, NOT auto-blocked. The new rule applies prospectively to newly approved carriers. No backfill-and-reject of the existing carrier base.
    - **Gate scope:** age derived ON READ from stored `authorityGrantedDate`. NOT a cron-refreshed `authorityAgeDays` snapshot. The `authorityAgeDays` schema field at [`schema.prisma:881`](backend/prisma/schema.prisma#L881) stays unused per locked decision — recomputing months from the stable grant date each gate fire is cheaper than maintaining a stale snapshot.
    - **Onboarding rejection UX (Option β):** carriers under 18 months at the `/onboarding` MC/DOT lookup are NOT hard-rejected. Their email + DOT + projected eligibility date are captured to a new `WaitingList` Prisma model; an auto-notify fires when they cross 18 months. No "Application rejected" dead-end page.
    - **Soft authority-age deduction in `carrierVettingService.ts:249-265`:** retained as-is. The hard gate subsumes the block decision; the vetting score deduction remains for analytics + Compass Score continuity. Revisit at v3.8.ahn close to decide whether to remove the now-redundant soft check.

    **FMCSA data source.** Free QCMobile endpoint `GET /qc/services/carriers/{dot}/authority?webKey={key}` using the existing `FMCSA_WEB_KEY` env var. Earliest `original_served_date` from the operating-authority history is the canonical grant date. Sub-rule c verification (web research 2026-05-21): endpoint exists per FMCSA QCMobile documentation; free under the same webKey the service already holds; response shape includes `docket_number`, `authority_type`, `original_action`, `original_served_date`, `disposition_action`, `disposition_served_date` per Alphaloops 2026 FMCSA API reference. The endpoint is NOT documented on the `/QCDevsite/docs/apiElements` page but IS listed on the `/QCDevsite/docs/qcApi` endpoint inventory.

    **Reinstatement-continuity caveat (deferred).** A carrier whose authority was granted, revoked, and later reinstated reads as older than they operationally are because the gate anchors on the original grant date, not the most recent reinstatement. Deliberate v3.8.ahj decision: anchor on `original_served_date` for now and document the edge case for an eventual AE-warning surface in v3.8.ahl or v3.8.ahm window. Not a v3.8.ahj fix.

    **Sprint sequence (each atomic per §3.3; halt for ratification between each):**
    - **v3.8.ahj — FMCSA authority data plumbing.** New `getCarrierAuthority(dotNumber)` in `fmcsaService.ts` hitting the QCMobile authority endpoint. New `fmcsaTypes.ts` with `FMCSAAuthorityResult` interface. Parallel `authorityCache` map (inherits the service's existing 1-hour TTL — the epic-design assumption was 24h but Pattern 6 sub-rule c authoritative-source verification confirms the existing pattern is 1h; refactor to per-key TTL is out of v3.8.ahj scope). Smoke test with mocked `fetch` covering happy path / no-history / multi-GRANT-earliest-wins / REVOCATION-REINSTATEMENT-ignored. **No schema write-path, no gate, no override UI, no onboarding integration in this sprint.** ~250 LOC.
    - **v3.8.ahk — Schema population.** `registerCarrier` controller calls `getCarrierAuthority` during registration, persists `authorityGrantedDate` on `CarrierProfile` (field already exists at [`schema.prisma:880`](backend/prisma/schema.prisma#L880), currently unpopulated). One-time backfill script for existing APPROVED carriers (each carrier hit once; cached locally; idempotent). Leave `authorityAgeDays` unused per locked decision. ~80 LOC + backfill script.
    - **v3.8.ahl — Hard gate in `complianceCheck()`.** New check #14 in `complianceMonitorService.ts` between insurance-expiry and FMCSA-authority-status. Returns `{ blocked: true, code: "AUTHORITY_TOO_YOUNG", overridable: bool, ageMonths: N }` with `overridable=true` iff `ageMonths ∈ [12, 18)`. Soft-grandfather flag for carriers whose `approvalDate < v3.8.ahl ship date` — AE warning, not block. ~60 LOC + vitest coverage.
    - **v3.8.ahm — Override flow + AE UI.** Extends existing `OverrideComplianceModal.tsx` to handle the new `AUTHORITY_TOO_YOUNG` block code. Override reason capture includes the age-months at override time. Same 24h expiry + 15/30-day quota. ~120 LOC.
    - **v3.8.ahn — Onboarding UI + WaitingList.** New `WaitingList` Prisma model (`{ id, email, dotNumber, mcNumber?, authorityGrantedDate, eligibilityDate, notifiedAt?, createdAt }`). Carrier-self-service `/onboarding` MC/DOT lookup surfaces verdict (auto-allow / override-eligible / waiting-list-with-projected-eligibility-date).     **v3.8.ahl + v3.8.ahm status (this two-commit arc closes Item 182 sprint 3 of 5):** LOGGED + CLOSED. Hard authority-age gate shipped per the ratified Phase A decisions D7-D11. Shape:

    - **v3.8.ahl (commit 1):** scoped-override migration. The blanket short-circuit at [`complianceMonitorService.ts:41-55`](backend/src/services/complianceMonitorService.ts#L41) now filters on `checkCode IS NULL` only — scoped overrides (`checkCode != null`) do NOT trigger the blanket allow-all and are consulted per-check downstream. Sprint 40 quota (15 per rolling 30 days), 24h expiry, and ADMIN/CEO role gate untouched.

    - **v3.8.ahm (commit 2):** the gate itself. New `AUTHORITY_AGE_GATE_LIVE_AT` constant in [`complianceMonitorService.ts`](backend/src/services/complianceMonitorService.ts) — single source of truth for the grandfather cutoff (hardcoded per Phase A D8-S, not env-driven). Currently set to `2026-05-21T19:00:00Z` placeholder; Wasi confirms exact value before push. Gate slotted between insurance-expiry (lines 62-70) and FMCSA authority-STATUS (lines 73-81). `calendarMonthsBetween` exported from [`fmcsaService.ts`](backend/src/services/fmcsaService.ts) for reuse — same helper from v3.8.ahj, no duplication.

    **Logic (D9-U + hard floor at 12 ratified):**
    - `approvedAt < AUTHORITY_AGE_GATE_LIVE_AT` → grandfather (warning, never block, regardless of age or null grant).
    - `approvedAt >= cutoff` + `authorityGrantedDate` present + `ageMonths >= 18` → silent allow.
    - `approvedAt >= cutoff` + `12 <= ageMonths < 18` → block by default, **released** by an active `ComplianceOverride` with `checkCode = "AUTHORITY_TOO_YOUNG"`. Override release surfaces an `AUTHORITY_AGE_OVERRIDE` warning.
    - `approvedAt >= cutoff` + `ageMonths < 12` → **HARD FLOOR — block always, no override consulted** (override is NOT looked up in this branch, deliberate per Phase A D9).
    - `approvedAt >= cutoff` + null grant + `<24h since approval` → warning only (`AUTHORITY_PENDING`).
    - `approvedAt >= cutoff` + null grant + `>=24h since approval` → hard block (`AUTHORITY_UNVERIFIED`).

    **Block strings coded per D10-Z** for downstream frontend pattern-matching: `"AUTHORITY_TOO_YOUNG: carrier authority N months old, minimum 18"`, `"AUTHORITY_UNVERIFIED: FMCSA authority could not be verified — contact compliance"`. Warning strings prefixed `"AUTHORITY_AGE_GRANDFATHERED: ..."`, `"AUTHORITY_AGE_OVERRIDE: ..."`, `"AUTHORITY_PENDING: ..."`.

    **D11 — carrierVettingService soft check left unchanged.** [`carrierVettingService.ts:249-265`](backend/src/services/carrierVettingService.ts#L249) still deducts 5-10 vetting-score points for authority <180 days. Revisit at the renumbered v3.8.aho close (Onboarding+WaitingList sprint, originally ahn).

    **Test coverage:** new [`backend/__tests__/unit/services/complianceMonitorService.test.ts`](backend/__tests__/unit/services/complianceMonitorService.test.ts) with 9 cases — all 7 ratified scenarios plus a 1b subtest for grandfather-with-young-authority and a 3a/3b split on the 12-18 month window. `vi.useFakeTimers()` + `vi.setSystemTime(FIXED_NOW)` pin "now" to a deterministic mid-month date (2026-06-15T12:00:00Z, ~25 days past the gate cutoff) so calendar-month arithmetic produces exact ages via an `nMonthsAgo(N)` helper. `vi.resetAllMocks()` in `beforeEach` clears the `mockResolvedValueOnce` queue between tests — a defensive change after debugging surfaced a Once-mock leak from case 4 polluting case 5's blanket-override lookup (banked as a sub-rule c learning: when mocking the SAME function multiple times across tests, the Once-queue must be reset, not just cleared).

    **Epic re-letter — the two-commit shape consumed an extra letter:** the originally-planned v3.8.ahm (Override flow + AE UI) and v3.8.ahn (Onboarding UI + WaitingList) sprints will be assigned the next available letters at their respective kickoff times, based on what's free in the v3.8.* sequence then. 185. **Daily `fmcsaComplianceScan` cron runs in UTC, not Eastern.** Banked 2026-05-22 alongside v3.8.ahw close. Phase A read-only finding: no `cron.schedule()` call in [`backend/src/cron/index.ts`](backend/src/cron/index.ts) passes a `timezone` option (Phase A grep `timezone` case-insensitive across the file returned zero hits). `node-cron` default behavior: uses host process's local time. `render.yaml` has no `TZ` env var (Phase A grep `TZ|timezone|timeZone` returned zero hits). Render Linux containers default to UTC unless `TZ` is set. **Net effect:** the `"0 3 * * *"` daily FMCSA scan fires at **3:00 AM UTC**, which is 11:00 PM Eastern (during EDT) or 10:00 PM Eastern (during EST) — same evening, prior calendar day from a US-ops perspective. All other "daily AM" jobs in the same file (`daily-cpp-cleanup 6am`, `health-digest 7am`, `compliance-reminders 5am`, identity-validation `6am`, ai-rate-intelligence `4am`, ai-carrier-intelligence `4:15am`, ai-compliance-forecast `5:30am`, ai-morning-briefing `6:30am`) inherit the same UTC default and similarly fire in the prior-day Eastern evening. This is operationally consistent across the cron file (all "daily" jobs run on the same wall clock), just not on the wall clock Wasi would intuit if reading "3 AM" as Eastern. **Sprint shape:** decide canonical for the whole cron file — either (a) accept UTC as the operational convention and document the offset in CLAUDE.md so future readers don't trip, OR (b) set the file's `cron.schedule()` calls to pass `{ timezone: "America/New_York" }` (or `"America/Detroit"` per §1 principal address) so cron times read as Eastern, OR (c) set `TZ=America/New_York` on the Render service env so the whole process clock shifts (also affects log timestamps + any `new Date()` formatting in user-facing emails). Decision pending Wasi call. Effort: small (~5 LOC + a Render dashboard env edit). Not BKN-blocking — FMCSA scan firing at 11pm ET vs 3am ET produces the same operational outcome (overnight refresh either way), just changes when the scan's email-to-admins surfaces in Wasi's inbox.

186. **`ComplianceScan` rows have no in-app view; `ComplianceAlert` does.** Banked 2026-05-22 alongside v3.8.ahw close. Phase A read-only finding from grep `ComplianceScan|ComplianceAlert|complianceAlert|complianceScan` across `frontend/src/`: **2 admin-UI consumers, both on the alert side, none on the scan side.** (a) [`frontend/src/app/dashboard/violations/page.tsx`](frontend/src/app/dashboard/violations/page.tsx) — declares a local `ComplianceAlert` interface (line 44) and queries `GET /compliance/alerts` (line 84). This is the real AE-facing surface for compliance alerts. (b) [`frontend/src/components/dashboard/CeoOverview.tsx`](frontend/src/components/dashboard/CeoOverview.tsx) — reads CRITICAL + WARNING alert counts from a summary endpoint (lines 217, 365), surfaces them as a TeamMetricRow tile only. **`ComplianceScan` rows have ZERO frontend readers.** They land in the database (full FMCSA snapshot + previous-data + changes-detected JSON per carrier per scan) and feed downstream comparisons inside `fmcsaComplianceScan` itself, but no admin UI displays scan history. Net: change history is queryable via SQL/Prisma only. **Sprint shape:** if AE/CEO wants visibility into "what changed on this carrier across the last N FMCSA scans," need a new surface — either (a) a `ComplianceScan` history tab inside the existing `/dashboard/violations` page filterable by carrier, OR (b) a per-carrier expandable section in the existing CarrierDrawer / CarrierDetailDrawer showing the last K scans with their `changesDetected` JSON unrolled, OR (c) a CSV export endpoint for periodic review without an in-app surface. Effort varies by choice; (b) is the lowest-LOC option (~80-120 LOC, single file). Not urgent — the alerts surface already shows the operationally-actionable signal (critical / warning entries); scan history is forensic / audit value only. **Pairs with Item 8.9** (authority-block centralization) loosely as compliance-observability infrastructure cleanup; not the same class.

187. **Suspension-column convention unification across `complianceMonitorService.ts`.** Banked 2026-05-22 alongside v3.8.ahw close — promoted from the scope-corrected TODO comment at [`complianceMonitorService.ts:810-820`](backend/src/services/complianceMonitorService.ts#L810). Two suspension-reason/timestamp column pairs are both live on `CarrierProfile` and both written by the canonical compliance service: (a) **`autoSuspendReason` + `autoSuspendedAt`** — the newer pair, written by `fmcsaComplianceScan`'s revoke / insurance-missing / OOS branches (lines ~947, ~1058) AND by the Sprint 40 `OverrideComplianceModal` cleanup query at line ~1225 which uses `autoSuspendedAt` as the lookup key for clearing override-stale entries. (b) **`suspensionReason` + `suspendedAt`** — the older pair, written by 4 OTHER canonical-service branches: insurance-expiry handler (line ~1424), monthly re-vetting (line ~1553), FMCSA authority-change watcher (line ~1662), FMCSA safety-rating watcher (line ~1702). **Correctness impact today: low.** `complianceCheck` at line 115 keys off `onboardingStatus === "SUSPENDED"` only — neither reason/timestamp column gates anything. The drift is observability noise: when an AE looks at why a carrier got auto-suspended, the explanation lives in one column or the other depending on which code path triggered, and any UI / report that reads only one column will silently skip half the suspensions. **Recommended canonical: `autoSuspendReason` + `autoSuspendedAt`.** Reasons: (i) used by Sprint 40 OverrideComplianceModal infrastructure, (ii) more semantically explicit (`auto` prefix surfaces that the system, not a human, did the suspending), (iii) only 4 call sites need to migrate vs 5+ surfaces if we picked the older pair. **Sprint shape:** rename across the 4 older-pair writers above + verify no admin UI / Prisma query reads the older pair (grep `suspensionReason|suspendedAt` across `backend/` + `frontend/` first). One-time data backfill SQL to migrate existing rows where the older pair is set but the newer is null. ~30-60 LOC source + 1 backfill script. Defensible to defer until either (a) an AE-facing surface starts reading the columns and the inconsistency becomes user-visible, OR (b) the platform takes any other action on `CarrierProfile.suspensionReason`/`suspendedAt` (e.g. adding it to a search / export, or removing it). Not BKN-blocking — pre-revenue carrier count means most auto-suspensions today are the FMCSA branches that already use the newer pair.

No schema migration. Pairs with Build 3 as the Tier 2 + Tier 3 split. Same boundary discipline as Build 1: only addition is `isTestAccount: false`. Pattern 7 grep-completeness check: re-grep `prisma\.carrierProfile|prisma\.load.*carrier` to verify no Tier 2 site was missed.

191. **Prisma + Neon `DIRECT_URL` split — permanent fix for the P1002 advisory-lock contention class.** Banked 2026-05-24 alongside the v3.8.ajf P1002 incident (third fire in the v3.8.a* session arc — v3.8.ail, v3.8.aix, v3.8.ajf all hit `Timed out trying to acquire a postgres advisory lock (SELECT pg_advisory_lock(72707369))` after `prisma migrate deploy` started). **Root-cause characterization (now three-fire-validated):** Prisma's `migrate deploy` acquires a Postgres advisory lock (hardcoded `72707369` in Prisma source) before applying migrations. Lock is session-scoped — released only when the connection holding it actually closes. Today's `DATABASE_URL` env var on Render points at Neon's POOLED endpoint (hostname contains `-pooler`), which intentionally keeps connections alive between requests and rotates PIDs across the pool. Net effect: migrate process exits normally, but its lock-holder connection stays cached in Neon's pooler. Lock doesn't release until Neon's idle timer expires that specific cached PID (~5min on Launch tier). Every subsequent `migrate deploy` plays roulette against whichever pooler-cached PID currently holds the lock. P1002 frequency correlates with migration-bearing deploy frequency. **Permanent fix — canonical Prisma + Neon pattern documented by both vendors:** split runtime + migrate connection URLs. (a) `backend/prisma/schema.prisma` `datasource db { ... }` block adds `directUrl = env("DIRECT_URL")` line alongside existing `url = env("DATABASE_URL")`. (b) Render dashboard env var added: `DIRECT_URL` = Neon's direct endpoint connection string (no `-pooler` in hostname; obtained from Neon dashboard → Connection Details → "Direct connection" tab). (c) Local `backend/.env` adds the same `DIRECT_URL` for `prisma migrate dev` (when used in feature branches) + diagnostic `prisma migrate status` runs. (d) `DATABASE_URL` UNCHANGED — runtime continues to benefit from pooler's connection-limit management. Prisma automatically uses `directUrl` for ALL migrate operations (`migrate deploy`, `migrate dev`, `migrate status`, `migrate resolve`, `db push`) when present in the datasource block. Direct connection releases the advisory lock the moment migrate exits — no pooler caching layer between Prisma and Postgres. **Belt-and-suspenders secondary hardening (same sprint, ~5 min add):** `PRISMA_MIGRATE_LOCK_TIMEOUT=60000` env var on Render bumps Prisma's lock-acquisition timeout from 10s default to 60s. Reduces residual P1002 frequency on the direct URL itself (e.g. if Render somehow runs two concurrent deploys, which would normally serialize). **Side benefits beyond P1002 elimination:** (i) `prisma migrate status` becomes deterministic — currently it also runs through the pooler and can give stale answers about applied-vs-pending migrations; (ii) the Sprint 44b `prisma migrate status --exit-code` post-deploy verification gate becomes reliable instead of probabilistic; (iii) future destructive migrations (enum-swaps like v3.8.ajd, column-drops, table-renames) become safer because the lock is held by a connection that genuinely owns the migration. **Risks considered + rejected:** (a) `PRISMA_SCHEMA_DISABLE_ADVISORY_LOCK=1` env var — disables the lock entirely, allowing two concurrent migrate processes to apply destructive migrations simultaneously; an enum-swap class migration could corrupt under concurrent application; not recommended. (b) Pre-deploy SQL hook running `pg_advisory_unlock(72707369)` — race condition with legitimate concurrent migrations; would also fail if the lock-holder is a different PID than the unlock caller; not recommended. (c) Switching off Neon to RDS / Supabase / another managed Postgres — over-engineering for this specific class; the same pooler vs direct distinction exists on most managed Postgres providers and is solved the same way. **Sprint shape:** ~10 LOC schema change + 2 env var additions (Render dashboard + local `.env`) + 1 CLAUDE.md §2.2 documentation update noting the new env vars + their roles. Effort: 30-60 min, mostly Neon dashboard navigation + Render env editing. No migration. No code logic change. **Pre-commit verification:** `npx prisma migrate status` against direct URL should report `Database schema is up to date` before push. Post-deploy: next migration-bearing deploy should complete in <5s without P1002 even if a prior deploy was recent. **Priority:** ELEVATED — every future schema migration is at risk until this lands. Pairs naturally with §13.3 Item 8.10's deploy-chain hardening lineage (Sprint 44a → 44b → 44c → 44d) as the natural next architectural-hardening sprint. **Banked methodology observation:** Sprint 44b's baseline-reset + canonical buildCommand work hardened the migration history + verification gate but did NOT address the connection-URL split. The class of bug was latent through the entire Sprint 44 → ajf arc; three independent fires in <2 weeks validated the recurrence rate as material enough to justify the architectural fix vs continuing to absorb the manual-retry cost.

190. **Build 3 — `isTestAccount` fence extended to Tier 3 compliance surfaces.** Banked 2026-05-23 alongside v3.8.aim Build 1 close. Build 2 closes the analytics side; Build 3 closes the daily compliance scan + alert/forecast surfaces so test carriers don't pollute the compliance signal. Sites to fence (all in `backend/src/services/complianceMonitorService.ts` + adjacent): (a) [`complianceMonitorService.ts:319`](backend/src/services/complianceMonitorService.ts#L319) insurance-expiry sweep. (b) [`complianceMonitorService.ts:366`](backend/src/services/complianceMonitorService.ts#L366) expiring-soon items dashboard feed. (c) [`complianceMonitorService.ts:458-461`](backend/src/services/complianceMonitorService.ts#L458) generic compliance findMany. (d) **[`complianceMonitorService.ts:823`](backend/src/services/complianceMonitorService.ts#L823) `fmcsaComplianceScan` — the daily 3am scan over APPROVED carriers; highest-volume hit. Primary noise-reduction win.** (e) [`complianceMonitorService.ts:1130`](backend/src/services/complianceMonitorService.ts#L1130) monthly re-vetting cron sweep. (f) [`complianceMonitorService.ts:1240`](backend/src/services/complianceMonitorService.ts#L1240) suspended-carrier auto-recovery sweep. (g) [`complianceMonitorService.ts:1437`](backend/src/services/complianceMonitorService.ts#L1437) expired-insurance auto-suspend sweep. (h) [`complianceController.ts:173`](backend/src/controllers/complianceController.ts#L173) admin compliance list endpoint. (i) [`complianceForecastService.ts:41-42`](backend/src/services/complianceForecastService.ts#L41) AI compliance forecast. (j) [`chameleonDetectionService.ts:218`](backend/src/services/chameleonDetectionService.ts#L218) pairwise carrier-similarity check (filter both sides — test accounts shouldn't be matched against real carriers or each other). (k) [`cron/index.ts:144`](backend/src/cron/index.ts#L144) + [`cron/index.ts:347`](backend/src/cron/index.ts#L347) cron-driven carrier sweeps. **Sprint shape:** single atomic commit, ~22 LOC across ~7 files, or extract a shared `whereActiveProductionCarrier()` helper IF Build 2 + 3 reveal sufficient drift risk (decision deferred to Phase A on Build 3). Same boundary as Build 1 + 2: only addition is `isTestAccount: false`. Pattern 7 grep-completeness check before close: re-grep `prisma\.carrierProfile\.find` across `backend/src/` to verify every carrier-list site is now fenced through Build 1+2+3.

**Production reliability — hotfix (logged + closed 2026-05-06 in v3.8.aaf, Sprint 26b):**

32. ~~**Load Board click-to-detail React error #31 crash on loads with accessorials.**~~ **CLOSED 2026-05-06 in v3.8.aaf** (Sprint 26b hotfix between Sprint 26 close and Sprint 27 start). Surfaced during Sprint 26 Phase C smoke (creating test load via Order Builder → clicking load on Load Board → page crashed with full-screen "Something went wrong" + React error #31 "Objects are not valid as a React child"). Root cause: JSON column shape mismatch on `Load.accessorials`. Order Builder writes `Array<{type, amount, payer}>` per the [`Accessorial`](frontend/src/app/dashboard/orders/types.ts#L90) interface; convert-to-load endpoint at [`backend/src/routes/orders.ts:455`](backend/src/routes/orders.ts#L455) writes the form's array verbatim to the JSON column. Load Board side panel at [`loads/page.tsx:1030-1036`](frontend/src/app/dashboard/loads/page.tsx#L1030) (pre-fix) iterated `load.accessorials` with `key={a}` and rendered `{a}` directly — assuming `string[]` not `object[]`. React threw error #31 with the object's keys (type, amount, payer) in the error args. Latent since v3.8.c (Order Builder convert flow shipped ~Apr 28). Pre-commit tsc passed every sprint because the Zod validator at [`backend/src/validators/load.ts:113`](backend/src/validators/load.ts#L113) is `z.array(z.any()).optional()` — type-system can't catch JSON-column shape mismatches. **Trigger conditions** (all three required): load created via Order Builder convert flow, user added at least one accessorial before converting, user clicks the load on Load Board to open side panel. Loads without accessorials don't trigger (render gated on `length > 0`); loads created via Load Board's `+ New Load` 4-step modal don't trigger (no accessorial entry surface). **Fix shape — F2 per audit:** render `accessorial.type` with optional ` ($amount)` suffix. Defensive type-check handles three input shapes: `typeof a === "string"` (legacy data compat for any pre-v3.8.c string-only records) → render `a`; object with `type` key → render `"${a.type}${a.amount ? ` ($${a.amount})` : ""}"`; fallback → literal `"Accessorial"`. React `key` switched from `key={a}` (would have collided on repeat types) to `key={i}` (array index, stable for purely-visual list with no reorder). **Adjacent risk sweep cleared** (Phase A): Load model has 4 JSON columns total — stops (1112), accessorials (1146 — this bug), additionalRefs (1225), datPostedFields (1254). Only `accessorials` was rendered as a React child on the Load Board page; other JSON columns either aren't read or aren't rendered as children. One-finding fix, not class-wide cleanup. **Out of scope (deferred):** tightening Zod validator at `validators/load.ts:113` from `z.array(z.any())` to `z.array(z.object({type, amount, payer}))` — separate sprint; doesn't prevent future render-side bugs, just data-side. Audit of other JSON-column render sites across the codebase — broader audit sprint. **Pre-commit verification:** backend `tsc --noEmit` clean (no backend changes; verifying nothing drifted), frontend `next build` clean. Net LOC change: ~10 (1 file, accessorials block rewritten with defensive type-check + index keying). Per §3.1 sequence-continuous rule: v3.8.aae → v3.8.aaf. Hotfix-with-immediate-close pattern (logged + closed in same commit) — used because the bug blocked Sprint 26 Phase C smoke verification. **Severity: P0** — every BOL printed in the system embeds a QR code that routes customers to a 404 when scanned. Same defect class affects email tracking links sent via `shipperLoadNotifyService`. **Smoking gun:** [`backend/src/utils/qrGenerator.ts:25`](backend/src/utils/qrGenerator.ts#L25) encodes URL `https://silkroutelogistics.ai/track/<12-char-token>`. Frontend has NO `/track/[token]/page.tsx` dynamic route ([`frontend/src/app/track/`](frontend/src/app/track/) contains only `page.tsx`, no `[token]` subdirectory). [`frontend/public/_redirects`](frontend/public/_redirects) has no `/track/*` splat rule. [`frontend/next.config.ts:5`](frontend/next.config.ts#L5) sets `output: "export"` (static HTML export — Cloudflare Pages serves static files only, no SSR fallback). Net result: Cloudflare Pages serves default 404 for any `/track/<anything>` path. **Email path same defect:** [`backend/src/services/shipperLoadNotifyService.ts:48`](backend/src/services/shipperLoadNotifyService.ts#L48) builds `${PORTAL_BASE}/tracking/${load.trackingToken}`. `_redirects` line 27 redirects `/tracking` (exact) → `/track` 301, but no rule for `/tracking/*` subpaths — 404 on the same Cloudflare Pages fallback. **Fix surface options:** (a) Add `frontend/src/app/track/[token]/page.tsx` dynamic route that reads `params.token` from path, auto-fills the search box, and auto-fires the API call on mount. Cleanest UX. Requires new file ~50-80 LOC + import path updates. (b) Add `_redirects` splat: `/track/* /track 200` (URL-rewrite, not 301) + read token from `useSearchParams` or `usePathname` on the existing static page; would require URL-param plumbing on the existing page. (c) Belt-and-suspenders: both. Plus `_redirects` rule `/tracking/* /track/:splat 301` to align email links with QR pattern. **Recommend (a) + email-link rewrite** — dynamic route handles QR pattern, separate email change makes `shipperLoadNotifyService` build `/track/<token>` instead of `/tracking/<token>` to consolidate on one URL pattern. **Verification:** after fix, scan a printed BOL QR with phone camera → should auto-load tracking page with token-driven results (no manual entry). Test with at least one ShipperTrackingToken from prod DB to confirm round-trip. **Discovery context:** Sprint 25 was scoped to contrast fix + 3-tab → 2-tab reduction on `/track`. The BOL QR 404 was an adjacent finding from auditing the data-model parity (where do "Tracking codes" come from, who distributes them) — turns out the answer is "they come from QR codes that don't work." **Bumps queue:** P0 production reliability outranks remaining brand polish work — recommend slotting this ahead of `/shippers` narrative work and other §13.3 items not currently blocking. **Effort estimate:** medium sprint, ~80-150 LOC (new dynamic route + URL-param plumbing + email link consolidation). Pairs naturally with §13.3 Item 6 (Portal Approval UI S-3) only insofar as both are customer-facing surface defects; otherwise standalone.
